From linux at frodo.hserus.net  Sat Sep 11 16:44:06 2004
From: linux at frodo.hserus.net (Suresh Ramasubramanian)
Date: Sat Sep 11 16:44:00 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Reg MX record help
In-Reply-To: <4142DD51.4040408@frodo.hserus.net>
References: <1094899978.7429.8.camel@localhost.localdomain>
	<4142DD51.4040408@frodo.hserus.net>
Message-ID: <4142DDFE.2010201@frodo.hserus.net>

Suresh Ramasubramanian wrote:
> Anyway I am able to resolve your MX records - so yahoo should be able to 
>  do this too - if not now at least a few hours later.

Oh wait, I'm an idiot

You have pointed amiindia.co.in's MX to venus.amiindia.co.in

;; ANSWER SECTION:
amiindia.co.in.         23h57m18s IN MX  10 venus.amiindia.co.in.

Problem is there is no A record for venus.amiindia.co.in pointing to the 
IP for your mailserver

So set an A record up -

venus.amiindia.co.in.		IN	A	your.ip.add.ress

Update the serial number of the zone for amiindia.co.in and then reload 
ndc to update your nameservers.

	suresh

>any issues regarding the speed of a web site interaction as the number
>of connections increase. I am designing a small college database and
>would at the maximum have 250 simultaneous connections (all the
>students logging in to check there results.as the system will most
>probably remain off line there will be a maximum of 250 local
>connecions i presume. However depending upon the feedback may have to
>put it on the main portal itself (which would be gr8) ). Would like to
>keep the system open to usage of both PostgreSQL. and MySQL.( Also
>would try to use something new :-)
>
>Also I have used MySQL and am now shifting to PostgreSQL. Would like
>to know why it is not such a common platform with PHP. Guess speed is
>1 factor. But after that i think PostgreSQL is more feature rich.
>
>  
>
Should I use MySQL  or PostgreSQL?

Well then Yahoo uses MySQL.  I dont see any reason why
you should go for PostgreSQL.

Should I use PEAR DB Connectivity?

Well if you want maximum performance then don't.  If you want
to switch over to some other database i.e PostgreSQL in future then
go with Abstraction Layers.  Its the compromise you have to make
between speed and maintainability.

HTH

Karthikeyan B

Dear Ramnraj and Bharathi
Greetings !
Thank you for care on school education. 
The Matric. syllabus is discussed in a systematic way,
last week group of teachers had a seminor at CBE under Pro. Gnanam and
discussed the issues.
At present Our Educaiton system is based on Marks
you have to score the maximum possible marks.
it is because, we are unable to come to a common understanding on the 
Evaluvation system. Whether it is Objective Type Questions, or Descriptive 
Type or Continuous internal assesment or Practical Exams.
More over, we have to test on all the above to have a better understanding   
about student.

well, The text book should be prepared in a manner that it will help the 
students to understand the subject.
Teacher training is another aspec

Recently the 11th std, books are revised and published. we had the same level 
of discussions , we got the books late, students changedthe group because of 
the size of the book.

i have introduced StarOffice in 6th and 7th , but it has become a failure, 
because the students are unable to practise at home. 

As you mentioned, we have to introduce the Conepts like, WordProcessing, 
SpreadSheet, Database, web browser rather than brand name.  But because of 
the examination presser, the students forget. [ most of the Matric. schools, 
did not allow the students to learn, but they have to complete the portion ]


here are some of the positive impacts of the new syllabus.

1) Tamil Computing, 
2) latest topics like call centers, atm , VoIP,etc
3) Linux file system.
4) Internet related applications

here are some of the realities.

1)The salay of the Computer Teachers are very low [ around 2000 /- ] , that 
leads to lack of motivation.
2) the computer teachers are forced to do school office clerical work [ in the 
name of computerization ] to get a better certificate from the HM
3) Some or not qualified teachers
4) Many did not under go Bacheler of education, so they did not understand the 
students psycology.
5) The management may not support to upgrade the hardware and software.
[ many teachers did not know how to write in CD and how to configure email 
client or internet connections ]
6) the teachers are not encouraged to update [ permission will be denied to 
study further ]
7)Most of the computer teachers are still thinking that oneday they will join 
in a multinational company

i have few more realities, which i can not share in a public list like this.

in matriculation shcools, the conditions are far better. many ofthe  above 
points are void. but you have to add another point "ego"

more in next
thiagu

note: since this discussion is restricted to very few, we can have one-to one 
discussions, rather then mailing to the list.

Subject: [Ilugc] 2.6 kernel (debian) error
Message-ID: <3779a1e70409120001745089c2@mail.gmail.com>

I got a kernel panic while trying to boot the new 2.6 kernel.
Thought of usual things and did a mkinitrd and later compiled ext3
support into the kernel. But nothing seems to solve the problem.

But what is more confusing is this :along with the error message, I
was suggested to look into the 'root=' option in lilo.conf.

my lilo.conf:
------------------------------------------
prompt
boot=/dev/hda3
default=Linux
delay=40
root=/dev/hda3
install=/boot/boot.b
map=/boot/map
image=/vmlinuz.old
	label=Linux
	initrd=/initrd.old
image=/vmlinuz
	label=Linux2.6.8
--------------------------------------------

When I looked into this I was surprised!!! Because here is my fstab

--------------------------------------------
# /etc/fstab: static file system information.
#
# <file system> <mount point>   <type>  <options>       <dump>  <pass>
/dev/hda2	/	ext3	defaults,errors=remount-ro	0 1
/dev/fd0	/floppy	auto	rw,user,noauto	0 0
/dev/hdc	/cdrom	auto	ro,user,noauto	0 0
proc	/proc	proc	defaults	0 0
--------------------------------------------
where hda2 is mounted as root. But in my lilo.conf it is different.
When I changed it to hda2 in lilo.conf, I got kernel panic for both
the kernels.

Am I missing something here???

From sridharinfinity at gmail.com  Sun Sep 12 18:39:01 2004
From: sridharinfinity at gmail.com (Sridhar R)

Subject: [Ilugc] Ilugc Website - wiki?
Message-ID: <8816fcf80409120609718432b@mail.gmail.com>

I suggest using a wiki [1] in place of our existing website.  The advatages - 

1. No need to worry about administration
2. Anyone (at-least can restrict to ilugcians) can edit it
3. Anyone can put content into it.
4. Imagine the 'CDs for sale' page keep growing as users keep adding
the info. about the CDs they have
5. No centralized adminstration.  A set of people can become the SysOp
and monitor the changes
6. Just use the RSS of 'Recent Changes' for monitoring changes, you
(admin) don't need to visit the 'Recent changes' page daily to find
culprits.

I guess it make sense for us to use the wiki.  We don't need to ask
the list 'whether anyone is taking over the job of maintaining
website'. The point is everyone maintains the website (in their free
time) and the wiki helps them to do so, without much frills.

Please give me access to www.chennailug.org server, I will
install/configure mediawiki and let you all know.

See www.gentoo-wiki.com for an example. *We* can also put technical
articles, FAQs and virtually any kind of document in it

[1] http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wiki

--

> I got a kernel panic while trying to boot the new 2.6 kernel.
> Thought of usual things and did a mkinitrd and later compiled ext3
> support into the kernel. But nothing seems to solve the problem.
> 
> But what is more confusing is this :along with the error message, I
> was suggested to look into the 'root=' option in lilo.conf.
> 
> my lilo.conf:
> ------------------------------------------
> prompt
> boot=/dev/hda3
> default=Linux
> delay=40
> root=/dev/hda3
> install=/boot/boot.b
> map=/boot/map
> image=/vmlinuz.old
>        label=Linux
>        initrd=/initrd.old
> image=/vmlinuz
>        label=Linux2.6.8
> --------------------------------------------
> 
> When I looked into this I was surprised!!! Because here is my fstab
> 
> --------------------------------------------
> # /etc/fstab: static file system information.
> #
> # <file system> <mount point>   <type>  <options>       <dump>  <pass>
> /dev/hda2       /       ext3    defaults,errors=remount-ro      0 1
> /dev/fd0        /floppy auto    rw,user,noauto  0 0
> /dev/hdc        /cdrom  auto    ro,user,noauto  0 0
> proc    /proc   proc    defaults        0 0
> --------------------------------------------
> where hda2 is mounted as root. But in my lilo.conf it is different.
> When I changed it to hda2 in lilo.conf, I got kernel panic for both
> the kernels.
> 
> Am I missing something here???

> 
> I suggest using a wiki [1] in place of our existing website.  The advatages -
> 
> 1. No need to worry about administration
> 2. Anyone (at-least can restrict to ilugcians) can edit it
> 3. Anyone can put content into it.
> 4. Imagine the 'CDs for sale' page keep growing as users keep adding
> the info. about the CDs they have
> 5. No centralized adminstration.  A set of people can become the SysOp
> and monitor the changes
> 6. Just use the RSS of 'Recent Changes' for monitoring changes, you
> (admin) don't need to visit the 'Recent changes' page daily to find
> culprits.
> 
> I guess it make sense for us to use the wiki.  We don't need to ask
> the list 'whether anyone is taking over the job of maintaining
> website'. The point is everyone maintains the website (in their free
> time) and the wiki helps them to do so, without much frills.
> 
> Please give me access to www.chennailug.org server, I will
> install/configure mediawiki and let you all know.
> 
> See www.gentoo-wiki.com for an example. *We* can also put technical
> articles, FAQs and virtually any kind of document in it
> 
> [1] http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wiki
>

Subject: [Ilugc] C pgm - Recursive -segmentation fault 
Message-ID: <BC6E2BCE16A9D511933F00508BAED7C308EA88AD@ctp.satyam.com>



When I run this program, Recursive Function R(),

Called only 523714 times, after that segmentation fault occurs WHY?

void R()
{
    static int i =0;
    i++;
    printf("%d\n",i);

    R();
}

int main()
{
    R();
}

What is the problem here?

From praveen at symonds.net  Mon Sep 13 17:15:33 2004
From: praveen at symonds.net (Praveen)
Date: Mon Sep 13 17:16:51 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] C pgm - Recursive -segmentation fault
In-Reply-To: <BC6E2BCE16A9D511933F00508BAED7C308EA88AD@ctp.satyam.com>
References: <BC6E2BCE16A9D511933F00508BAED7C308EA88AD@ctp.satyam.com>
Message-ID: <4145885D.6030808@symonds.net>

Chakravarthi_Mohan wrote:


> 
> void R()
> {
>     static int i =0;
>     i++;
>     printf("%d\n",i);
> 
>     R();
> }
> 
> int main()
> {
>     R();
> }
> 
> What is the problem here?

For any recursive function, you should have an exit criteria. Otherwise 
it would recurse forever. Your function doesn't have an exit point.

> When I run this program, Recursive Function R(),
> Called only 523714 times, after that segmentation fault occurs WHY?

Since you don't have an exit point, repeated call of the function by itself 
leads to stack overflow.

HTH.

Probably you're out of memory (call stack)!
Any good recursive function should exit at some point in time say for
example:

void R()
{
	/* ... */
	if (i > 1000) return;
	/* ... */
}

Kannan_Ranganathan wrote:

>Consider a case where my program does something repeatedly ..in such a case
>I write a recursive program .what's the point in writing a recursive
>function if it is going to exit abruptly.

If you want to do something repeatedly, your program should have been...

void R()
{
    static int i =0;
    i++;
    printf("%d\n",i); 
}

int main()
{
  while(1)
    R();
}

This is what a daemon is.

From rudyandlinda at yahoo.com  Sun Sep 12 21:33:32 2004
From: rudyandlinda at yahoo.com (Rudy Colbert)
Date: Mon Sep 13 20:31:51 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] dual opteron
Message-ID: <20040913043332.19547.qmail@web52503.mail.yahoo.com>

==>I'm curious to hear if anybody has tried out a
64-bit x86-64 install of
any standard distro, and what their experiences
were.<==



Dual opteron planar boards available
from Tyan, Iwill, MSI and Rioworks 
are Extended ATX form factor (12"x13").
All of these boards require EPS12v
powersupply of min. 470w, preferred 550w.
They must have 24/8 power connectors
not the usual 20/4 power connectors.
In addition, thermal requirements 
require proper ventillation to keep 'em
running for a longtime.  All these
means you need to shop for the proper
system case and pretty good ceramic fans.

Now, the memory needs to be buffered, ecc
atleast ddr 2100.  'buffered, ecc' is a
requirement for Tyan board to boot everytime.
No cheap memories, choice is Micron, Samsung
and Kingston.  You can get 12gb to 32gb
depending on the planar board.  There are
several variations of planar boards.
Mostly, variations are in PCI-X bus 100 or 133, how
many, onboard Ultra Scsi or Sata etc.  Most come
with USB (most support 1.1 not 2.0)
Most planar boards comes with gigabit 
network interface(s), IDE & Floppy.

Now, that said here is a breakdown of 
discounted web prices from reliable vendors.
Planar $430, CPU 240 ($175 ea), Cooler ($30 ea),
EPS12v power ($100), 1gb ecc. reg memory ($240 ea)
EATX case ($120). So, dual opteron BYOS cost well
over $1500.

Now, having tested Tyan, Iwill & MSI, our preference
for our own warped reasons is MSI or Iwill. 
MSI was the reference board at AMD with long
visibility.
SCSI, SATA are pci board options.  Qlogic 2200 FC HBA
works on all planar boards we tested. We prefer this
to 
on-board for various reasons, a simple one
the onboard SATA doesn't support raid 5.

We have tested Fedora Core 2, Suse 9.1 Pro,
RedHat AS 3, and in the pipe SUSE SLES 9.
Fedora had no problem finding itself and
doing the right thing.
So are the Suse 9.1 and RedHat AS.

Where is the beef ? Almost, all versions 
had problems greater than 6gig configuration.
It works most of the time on RedHat and Suse.
We suspect it is more of a hardware problem.
Our initial deployment of 20 something
systems will have only 4Gig. So, to keep our sanity
we are not banging our head against barriers!
These systems will replace ibm pseries 660, 640
smp systems and AIX5.1L. In phase 1 we are
deploying some of these boxes to support >800 users
in a HA SAMBA/SAN environment and the other Oracle
custom apps.

To be fair, IBM brought some Boca boys and Austin
aunts, with their iSeries boxes.  We were blown away
by the Linux performance and price/performance value
of ibm's iseries boxes.

Now, we are scratching our head about phase 2. 
The iseries boxes benefits greatly from
the new power chip and its large cache in steps and
custom memory & bus management architecture. To add
to the 'value' computation ibm's support of system
and in SAN environment. 

Dual Opteron with SuSE/RH enterprise server software
is a good deal for startups, research institutes etc.,

In closing, it is not wise to compromise on
power-supply, cooler and memory.  They are part of the
equation for reliablity.  

Cheers,
Rudy

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Sun Sep 12 00:06:13 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar Babu)
Date: Mon Sep 13 23:45:02 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] C pgm - Recursive -segmentation fault
In-Reply-To: <FA3F4D4380B5D51186D600B0D0AAD2420A3BCB24@ccr.satyam.com>
References: <FA3F4D4380B5D51186D600B0D0AAD2420A3BCB24@ccr.satyam.com>
Message-ID: <20040912000613.0b8800d7.lug@chandrashekar.info>

> But tell me an recursive function shld run forever(atleast in theory) right
> ??? 

Perhaps you are trying to use a structured programming language to implemented a functional programming paradigm. If you are inclined towards writing programs using intoxicating amounts of recursion, you must either be writing them using haskell or LISP. But then, they too have their limitations. Any recursive block must end at some point either by a condition-check, or run till your system bails out of memory (or stack-space, precisely).

> Consider a case where my program does something repeatedly ..in such a case
> I write a recursive program .what's the point in writing a recursive
> function if it is going to exit abruptly.

If your task is to run a function repeatedly forever, you must redesign the function using iterative constructs (using while(), for(), do() or *gasp* goto, in C).

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.
From lug at chandrashekar.info  Sun Sep 12 00:11:57 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar Babu)

For all I know, this code isn't designed to run in the background on its own, it doesn't detached from the controlling terminal, and it also doesn't have any form of event-loop mechanism (which I believe are minimal requirements for calling a program a daemon).

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

From lokeswarab at hotmail.com  Tue Sep 14 04:19:12 2004
From: lokeswarab at hotmail.com (ragesh kannan)
Date: Tue Sep 14 09:58:59 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] C pgm - Recursive -segmentation fault
Message-ID: <BAY15-F26RtHTW5Lgp90001785c@hotmail.com>



Hi,
     The program design is wrong.     Anyway if you the reason for your 
program termination.
Normally the maximum stack size for the program is 8 MB.

     You can get this by

        #include<sys/resource.h>
       #define MB 1024*1024
       main()
        {
        struct rlimit rm;
        getrlimit(RLIMIT_STACK,&rm);
        printf("\nSTACK SIZE: MAX=%d MB CURR=%d\n", 
rm.rlim_max/(MB),rm.rlim_cur/(MB));
       }

   If you want you program want to run some more time use setrlimit... It's 
advisable that the maximum stack limit must be 16 MB less than physical 
memory.


For writing daemon process make use of the library function daemon(int,int); 
( #include <unistd.h>)

Hope this will help you.

Regards,
-lok.

From: Gopalarathnam V. [mailto:gopalarathnam_v@yahoo.com]

Subject: RE: [Ilugc] C pgm - Recursive -segmentation fault

My question is why would you want to write such a program which does an
infinite recursive looping.

If your intention is to write a daemon program, it is much more complex
-- you need to detach from the terminal and ignore certain signals, etc.
You can get the skeleton daemon program either from Advanced UNIX
Programming Environment or by digging the web.

From praveen at symonds.net  Tue Sep 14 10:54:23 2004

Subject: [Ilugc] C pgm - Recursive -segmentation fault

References: <FA3F4D4380B5D51186D600B0D0AAD2420A3BCB2C@ccr.satyam.com>
Message-ID: <41468087.9040404@symonds.net>

Kannan_Ranganathan wrote:

> void R()
> {
>     static int i =0;
>     i++;
>   /*  printf("%d\n",i);*/
> 
>     R();
> }
> 
> int main()
> {
>     R();
> }
> 
> in my Home ...the same program which was sent earlier.
> 
> This program is still running well above 12 hrs (running since last night
> till I left for office this morning  ) ... My machine is a P2 /64 MB ram. 
> 
> I am sure it would have run more than 52K times ...Any clues what's
> happening here ??? No segmentation fault nothing .
> Don't exactly remember gcc version..

The earlier version of the program would have atleast run for some time, but 
yours (without printf) would have seg faulted immediately.

The reason is the there is no console operation (printf). So, the code will reach 
the stack overflow condition in a second or two while the one with printf will 
take some time to reach the same condition. 

I am sure that you are missing out something if it runs for more than 12 hours 
(Impossible) no matter your have 64MB or 64GB of memory. Cross check your 
sources.

-- 
Praveen Kumar
Web    : http://myriad-zero.net
Blog   : http://blog.myriad-zero.net

From karthick.sundararajan at wipro.com  Tue Sep 14 11:28:39 2004

Please don't believe TC for segmentation faults. It is not reliable in
segmentation faults area. Try this code:
#include <stdio.h>

void main()
{
	int *ptr = (int*)0;

	if(*ptr = 5)
	{
		printf("It worked");
	}
}

	To the best of my knowledge it works more times than not.

	I think that is because DOS gives the whole of the avaibale
memory for the program under execution.

	Also, the best that can be expected is that TC will get closed
in such cases.

	Cheers,
	Karthick S.
	Mobile Number: 9884025911
	Home Page: www.geocities.com/sksatyam

A guideline to avoid spam is not to mention the exact e-mail address 
directly on the mails that are going to be archived on the web. Since 
this mail is going to be archived on the web, some spider crawling 
through the web can parse this address and add it to the list of 
valid e-mail addresses. Use some cryptic form like thrayil AT gmail DOT com 
instead.

On Tue, Sep 14, 2004 at 02:21:45AM -0700, Mohan Raj wrote:
> mkinitrd -o initrd <kernel version>

mkinitrd -c -k 2.6.8.1 

[or whatever your kernel version is]

It'll create /boot/initrd.gz which you'd pass to grub / lilo as initrd

> I read something about /proc being replaced with sysfs. So I have that
> entry too in my fstab. What should I do?

Best bet would be to get a .config for a 2.6 debian kernel and use that as a
base for make menuconfig

> 
  I have a fully-configured box with DVD drive and Xine. You'll
need an audio amp with RCA input jacks (L & R), and a projector
with VGA input capable of 48 kHz hsync (most projectors can handle
this). Also keep a PS/2 KB & mouse handy.

  The only issue is that playback was somewhat jerky last time
(slow CPU). I'll try to fix it today with a 2.6 kernel - if it
doesn't work any better, you'll have to put up with the frame
drops.

  As an alternative, I have a notebook with DVD drive that works
fine with PowerDVD on Windows ME (blasphemy!).

  If there's any interest, send me a note to work out the logistics
to get to AU tomorrow. I'll probably need to set it up at least
90 minutes in advance, to check if it works. How do I get to the
CS dept., and is there parking available?

-Siva

From rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au  Wed Sep 15 00:39:44 2004
From: rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au (Raja Subramanian)
Date: Tue Sep 14 20:10:05 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] C pgm - Recursive -segmentation fault
In-Reply-To: <FA3F4D4380B5D51186D600B0D0AAD2420A3BCB2C@ccr.satyam.com>
References: <FA3F4D4380B5D51186D600B0D0AAD2420A3BCB2C@ccr.satyam.com>
Message-ID: <20040914143944.GB7828@pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au>

Hi,

Kannan_Ranganathan wrote:
> void R()
> {
>     static int i =0;
>     i++;
>   /*  printf("%d\n",i);*/
> 
>     R();
> }
> 
> int main()
> {
>     R();
> }
> 
> in my Home ...the same program which was sent earlier.
> 
> This program is still running well above 12 hrs (running since last night
> till I left for office this morning  ) ... My machine is a P2 /64 MB ram. 

Compiler optimisation is at work here.

Lookup "tail recursion elimination" in GCC docs or your favourite
compilers book.

IIRC, GCC can also to "tail call elimination".  Both of which can
eliminate the recursive function call and effectively turn it into a
loop.

Try compiling without optimisation using the -O0 gcc flag and observe the
results.  To see what exactly happens when you optimise, try gcc -S,
which will provide you the asm code.

- Raja

	<20040914143944.GB7828@pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au>
	<8816fcf8040914074620e6e431@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20040914152040.GC7828@pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au>

Hi,

Sridhar R wrote:
> AFAIK, when gcc is called with *no* command line options, *no*
> optimization will be done.

While this is usually the case, it need not always be true.
GCC's default options are listed in the 'specs' file.

The OP did not mention the gcc flags used, and we can only speculate.

I just found out that gcc-2.95 does not know how to optimize tail calls.
However gcc-3.3.4 -foptimize-sibling-calls option completely eliminates
the recursive call.  Look at the C code and associated asm -

void foo(void) {
    static int i;
    i++;
    foo();
}


gcc -S test.s produces the following -

foo:
    pushl   %ebp
    movl    %esp, %ebp
    incl    i.0
    call    foo             <=== Function call!
    popl    %ebp
    ret


gcc -foptimize-sibling-calls -S test.c generates the following asm.

foo:
    pushl   %ebp
    movl    %esp, %ebp
.L3:
    incl    i.0
    jmp     .L3                 <=== Just a jump to L3

Note that this has eliminated tail recursion, and not just the sibling
call.  Good stuff.


- Raja

A recursive program runs as long as there is space in the stack.

It the recursion has been eliminated, maybe using "tail recursion
elimination", the generated executable is not recursive, and so runs
forever.

Please try this program and see what happens.

int R()
{
	static int i = 0;
	R();
	i++;
}

int main()
{
	R();
	return 0;
}

From rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au  Wed Sep 15 01:58:37 2004
From: rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au (Raja Subramanian)
Date: Tue Sep 14 21:28:48 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] C pgm - Recursive -segmentation fault
In-Reply-To: <FA3F4D4380B5D51186D600B0D0AAD2420A3BCB4B@ccr.satyam.com>
References: <FA3F4D4380B5D51186D600B0D0AAD2420A3BCB4B@ccr.satyam.com>
Message-ID: <20040914155837.GE7828@pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au>

Hi,

Kannan_Ranganathan wrote:
> Wow ..This is something new. infact the whole argument is centered on
> weather a recursive program will run forever or not.
> 
> Initially I had a belief that a recursive program will run forever. After
> all these discussions I reconciled recursion is dependent on stack memory.

A recursive program without a base case will run forever.  It's just the
same as an infinite for/while/goto loop.  No big deal.

In C, each function call uses some stack space to store the return
address and local variables.  Therefore recursion will cause stack
growth (explosion rather) and terminate your process when stack space
is exhausted.

If you are careful, you can do recursion without growing your stack.
Then you can recurse forever.  Functional programming languages like
haskel, prolog, mercury have been good at this game for many years.

Note that you cannot eliminate *all* recursive calls.  You can only
eliminate recursive calls under special conditions,
eg.  tail recursion - recursive call is last statement in your function.

Compilers: Principles Techniques and Tools (aka Dragon Book) has a lot
of stuff for an ardent reader.

- Raja

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Tue Sep 14 21:20:26 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Tue Sep 14 21:42:15 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] C pgm - Recursive -segmentation fault
In-Reply-To: <FA3F4D4380B5D51186D600B0D0AAD2420A3BCB4B@ccr.satyam.com>
Message-ID: <20040914155026.9E7BD32C81@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> 
> Wow ..This is something new. infact the whole argument is centered on
> weather a recursive program will run forever or not.
> 
  Whether a program will run forever or not has nothing to do with 
recursion. Recursion is merely a mechanism that allows a function
(subroutine) to call itself. 

> Initially I had a belief that a recursive program will run forever. After
> all these discussions I reconciled recursion is dependent on stack memory.
> 
  I don't believe you've understood anything from the discussion. A program
that uses a recursive function call may or may not run forever - it has
nothing to do with recursion. 

  Likewise, the size of the stack has nothing to do with how long a recursive
program will run. There are recursive functions that use very little stack,
but have a running-time complexity that grows exponentially with the input
argument. An example would be depth-first minimax search of any
reasonable game tree, including Chess or Reversi. The search will take
longer than the age of the universe, although the maximum game tree size
in chess is strictly bounded in height (it's no more than about 4000 deep,
probably even less when considering the 40-move endgame limit). It's
possible to write a recursive chess program that can exactly solve any
position, without running out of stack space; but it may take longer
than the age of the universe to run. 

> There were strong objections when I mentioned it was running well past 12
> hrs.

  You compiled it on a crappy real-mode DOS compiler that does not even
have memory protection or stack limits tests, and you actually believe
that your program was still running correctly without having completely
overwritten memory after the first few milliseconds? The strong objections
were more to do with the fact that you had no idea what you were doing.

> Whatever you have mentioned is quite contrary from rest of the post.
> Can you pls elaborate. 

  Raja was talking about tail-recursion elimination optimization in gcc,
and it's a special case where compilers can replace a recursive call
with a simple jump. There isn't any contradiction there - the asm code
shows the optimization quite clearly.

  What you need to do is read some introductory book on programming,
before filling this list with some more mindless blather.

-Siva

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Thu Sep 16 07:58:42 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Thu Sep 16 08:20:31 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Movie screening
In-Reply-To: <8816fcf8040914223777088116@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20040916022842.62ABA32C85@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>


  Just a few notes about the movie screening:

1) The venue was excellent - a spacious seminar hall with AV facility (this
could be a rough model for the kind of place to screen content in the
future. The turnout was pretty good, with an initial audience of about 100.
(About half the crowd left midway when we had media problems).

2) It helps to setup and test the equipment before the screening, including
a full run of the movie to check for media problems. In the event, the
Toshiba projector, the Xine source and the speakers worked better than
expected. However, the media problems in the second half of the movie
were unanticipated.

3) A break in the beginning/middle with a question-answer session would
also be useful. It so happened that we got that break accidentally when the
power went out :-). The question-answer session at the end, although
effective, did not have the full audience strength.

4) We need to replicate this experiment and repeat it at other venues after
sorting out the media problems. It helps to have backup media and/or
alternative content to show in the event of problems. However, it was
a useful learning experience.

5) It might be a good idea to have some ILUGC-related collateral to hand
out at the end (just a general printout with URLs, contacts, etc.), at least
in ILUGC-organized shows. We can also have standardized posters for The Code,
Revolution OS, ... that can be mailed out along with the invite to future
shows.

Sridhar & Vasudevan from the LUG regulars were present - others who showed
up at the demo day were also present. 

Further comments, suggestions, flames, etc. welcome.

-Siva

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Thu Sep 16 09:05:42 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Thu Sep 16 09:27:30 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] technical queries
In-Reply-To: <20040916033115.7692.qmail@web8503.mail.in.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20040916033542.2954A32C85@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> 1.what is a monolithic kernel.
>  
  Google is your friend. Monolithic is the
only choice you get if you want to use Linux/*BSD.

> 2.what is the memory -resolution tradeoff to be 
> followed while configuring the X server
> 
  It's no longer an issue. There's enough memory on today's
cards to support 32-bit depth at full resolution. The limitation
is in the monitor (CRT or LCD). The rule I follow is to use the
highest resolution I can comfortably see on my monitor with
minimal eye-strain. These are (on IBM CRT monitors, all at 16-bit
depth):

15": 800x600
17": 1024x768
19": 1280x1024
21": 1440x1080

The monitors can display much higher resolutions, but I don't use them. With
anti-aliased fonts, you can probably go one step higher without increased
eye-strain - YMMV.

My advice is to use virtual desktops or Xinerama if you want more display area,
rather than higher resolutions.

-Siva

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Thu Sep 16 09:38:12 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Thu Sep 16 10:00:01 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Xine configuration notes
Message-ID: <20040916040812.16B7D32C85@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>


   Just a summary of my Xine configuration (it's by no
means the only recipe for good results) on an Intel i815, Celeron 533
(8 x 66), 128 MB PC66 RAM, onboard graphics (should also work for the
ubiquitous i810 chipsets): 

1. Linux 2.6.8.1 with Deadline I/O scheduler (disable anticipatory,
CFQ, etc.)

2. ALSA compiled in, with OSS emulation. Disable OSS.

3. RedHat 7.3/9 distro w/ XFree86 4.2 or 4.3 w/ Xv extension (stock).

4. libdvdcss-1.2.8 (optional, only required for encrypted DVDs).

5. libdvdread-0.9.4 (from the ogle project)

6. Xine 0.9.13 (compiled with OSS and Xv support, built for i686-gnu-linux
   target).

7. dvdnav support with libdvdnav and xine-dvdnav.

8. Enable DMA and 32-bit I/O on the DVD drive with hdparm.

With this, I get the full 24/25 fps at 800x600 fullscreen with no audio dropouts
and perfect A/V sync on commercial DVDs without media faults (scratches, etc.).
There may be enough performance headroom to drop the CPU speed to 400/433
or increase the resolution to 1024x768 (both need to be tested).

TODO:

1. Alternative audio path (untested) using native ALSA with alsa-lib and Xine
built with ALSA support. 

2. Dolby 5.1 with AC3-to-SPDIF path on supported cards.

Comments invited from anybody who has experimented with similar or other
options.

-Siva

On Thu, 2004-09-16 at 09:01, NARASIMHAN LINUX wrote:
> 1.what is a monolithic kernel.

http://c2.com/cgi/wiki?MonolithicKernel

>  
> 2.what is the memory -resolution tradeoff to be 
>  
> followed while configuring the X server

Well, it depends on your monitor, if you have a 15" monitor, 1024x768
would be more than sufficient, and using a high quality display
definitely uses more memory.

The rule of the thumb is, it shouldn't be too much of a strain on your
eyes.

Configuring your monitor incorrectly might sometimes burn it, read the
manual accompanied for the horizontal sync and vertical refresh values.

The best possible way to configure XFree86 is by running XFree86
-configure, and then adjusting the parameters to suit your needs.

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Tue Sep 14 10:59:30 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar Babu)
Date: Thu Sep 16 10:38:08 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] technical queries - monitor resolutions
In-Reply-To: <1095310146.38080.8.camel@gopal-v.bangalore.corp.yahoo.com>
References: <20040916033115.7692.qmail@web8503.mail.in.yahoo.com>
	<1095310146.38080.8.camel@gopal-v.bangalore.corp.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20040914105930.50e6ec3b.lug@chandrashekar.info>

> Well, it depends on your monitor, if you have a 15" monitor, 1024x768
> would be more than sufficient, and using a high quality display
> definitely uses more memory.
>From what I know, most commodity 15" monitors (Samsung/LG/Daewoo and the
likes) can display 1024x768 resolution at 60Hz vertical refresh rate.
This refresh rate can cause eye-strain, fatigue and headache. 800x600 is
safest to use on these monitors. On a commodity 17" monitors however,
resolutions upto 1152x864 (at 75 Hz) seems safer to the eyes. 

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

From vaslin at gmail.com  Thu Sep 16 13:34:03 2004
From: vaslin at gmail.com (Vasudevan)
Date: Thu Sep 16 13:34:12 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Xine configuration notes
In-Reply-To: <20040916040812.16B7D32C85@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>
References: <20040916040812.16B7D32C85@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>
Message-ID: <f6a0291a0409160104465ed287@mail.gmail.com>

For Xine to work for dvd viewing  properly in Mdk 10 & Suse9.1

Add line

             Option       "XaaNoOffscreenPixmaps"
in
/etc/X11/XF86Config
in device section
or corresponding file in xorg


Enable DMA with command
hdparm -d1 /dev/dvd    (if /dev/dvd is your dvd drive)
Vasudevan


On Thu, 16 Sep 2004 09:38:12 +0530 (IST), Sivasankar Chander
<siva@dias.ath.cx> wrote:
> 
>    Just a summary of my Xine configuration (it's by no
> means the only recipe for good results) on an Intel i815, Celeron 533
> (8 x 66), 128 MB PC66 RAM, onboard graphics (should also work for the
> ubiquitous i810 chipsets):
> 
> 1. Linux 2.6.8.1 with Deadline I/O scheduler (disable anticipatory,
> CFQ, etc.)
> 
> 2. ALSA compiled in, with OSS emulation. Disable OSS.
> 
> 3. RedHat 7.3/9 distro w/ XFree86 4.2 or 4.3 w/ Xv extension (stock).
> 
> 4. libdvdcss-1.2.8 (optional, only required for encrypted DVDs).
> 
> 5. libdvdread-0.9.4 (from the ogle project)
> 
> 6. Xine 0.9.13 (compiled with OSS and Xv support, built for i686-gnu-linux
>    target).
> 
> 7. dvdnav support with libdvdnav and xine-dvdnav.
> 
> 8. Enable DMA and 32-bit I/O on the DVD drive with hdparm.
> 
> With this, I get the full 24/25 fps at 800x600 fullscreen with no audio dropouts
> and perfect A/V sync on commercial DVDs without media faults (scratches, etc.).
> There may be enough performance headroom to drop the CPU speed to 400/433
> or increase the resolution to 1024x768 (both need to be tested).
> 
> TODO:
> 
> 1. Alternative audio path (untested) using native ALSA with alsa-lib and Xine
> built with ALSA support.
> 
> 2. Dolby 5.1 with AC3-to-SPDIF path on supported cards.
> 
> Comments invited from anybody who has experimented with similar or other
> options.
> 
> -Siva
> 
> _______________________________________________
> To unsubscribe, email ilugc-request@ae.iitm.ac.in with
> "unsubscribe <password> address"
> in the subject or body of the message.
> http://www.ae.iitm.ac.in/mailman/listinfo/ilugc

From vsst at ipr.res.in  Thu Sep 16 13:27:32 2004

Subject: [Ilugc] Regarding DAT file copying in Linux
In-Reply-To: <20040916025037.2769A1DB296@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <Pine.GSO.4.10.10409161323080.648-100000@sun4.plasma.ernet.in>


    To copy a dat file, you can use cdrdao and then play it using mplayer.
         cdrdao read-cd --device=/dev/hdc --datafile mymovie.bin
         mplayer mymovie.bin will play the file.

From kaveraj at gmail.com  Thu Sep 16 15:17:27 2004
From: kaveraj at gmail.com (Mohan Raj)
Date: Thu Sep 16 15:17:35 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Debian mount point any diff from other distro ?
Message-ID: <3779a1e704091602471486b49@mail.gmail.com>

Is there any diff in the way debian labels partitions.

I have 3 primary partitions:

partition1 (ntfs) 
partition 2 (extended)
   extended partition 1 (ntfs)
   extended partition 2 (vfat)
partition 3 (ext3)

(I verified the above layout using qtParted)


(ntfs partitions are courtesy of OEM. I rarely use them anyway.
Yet to find time to put things in the right order).

Ok now here is the problem.
As you can see above, the ext3 partition should be labelled /dev/hda3. Right?
That is how it is in red hat (residing in another disk). But in
debian's fstab it is /dev/hda2.
I don't know how this has come to be. Making this more worse is
debian's lilo.conf
 which has root= options set to /dev/hda3. And that boots ok. Changing
it to hda2 results in a kernel panic. Interested to know what is
happening here...

-- 
 Mohan

lead in a couple of Linux projects, up-to-date with new developments, has
tinkered with Linux kernel (the core of the OS), enthusiastic, and good
communication.

Subject: [Ilugc] Installing NVIDIA display driver in MDK10
Message-ID: <20040917101521.76045.qmail@web41110.mail.yahoo.com>

My system is having NVIDIA RIVA TNT2 Model 64 display
driver. I am having 
problem in playing tuxracer and some other

games. I downloaded the following driver file from
nvidia site.

NVIDIA-Linux-x86-1.0-4496-pkg2.run

I understand, I need to run the file as root and make
necessary changes in 
the
/etc/X11/XF86Config file.

s having nvidia display, what changes I have to make
in the XF86Config-4

for the driver to load properly. Below I have
reproduced relevant section of 
my existing  XF86Config-4 file.

I would like to know from the Mandrake 10 users,what
changes I have to make 
in the XF86Config-4 file?

I read the latest kernel tested successfully was Red
Hat Linux version 
2.4.20-19.9 with the NVIDIA-Linux-x86-1.0-4496-pkg2.
Will this work properly 
in Mandrake 10 having kernel 2.6.*.*.

Thanks.

R.Dhanagopal


Section "Module"
    Load "dbe" # Double-Buffering Extension
    Load "v4l" # Video for Linux
    Load "extmod"
    Load "type1"
    Load "freetype"
    Load "glx" # 3D layer
EndSection


Section "Device"
    Identifier "device1"
    VendorName "nVidia Corporation"
    BoardName "RIVA TNT2"
    Driver "nv"
    Option "DPMS"
EndSection

Hi;
In case you are behind a proxy server and want to use gaim change the
port from 5050 to 25 and let the server name be scs.yahoo.com.
you can now continue using gaim !
the official version of yahoo messenger for linux is really bad.there
is a project to add video cam support for linux which is currently a
fork of gaim.once that project is stable it will be merged back to
the main tree.
needless to say contributions welcome :-)
K.Shyam

It will work with Netmeeting,
It dosent matter if you dont have a video device on either side,
Gnomemeeting works on H323 and an audio codec you could agree on

videoconferencing,
( will need to build Openh323 and Pwlib for ohphone )

We use ohphone for Embedded Video Conferencing boxes,

> otherwise quality will get affected. In skype this problem is not
> there. Incidenatlly this is the only voice chat client for linux at
> present.
> 
> Vasudevan

It's not the only voice chat client on linux. 
Look at http://www.phonegaim.com/

It's gaim modified to work with the SIP protocol - a  technology
competing with Skype.

haven't tried either, so can't comment on usability, etc.

It's funny though.. here we have IM clients perfectly capable of
transmitting text which can be typed on large comfortable keyboards
but we want to voice chat although the quality might be less than
stellar, the experience less than natural.

And then we have mobile phones where the device is perfectly capable
of transmitting crystal clear voice (well, usually!) but we want to
text chat by abusing our fingers typing SMSs on the most unintuitive
text input device possible.

funny world.

deepak.

-----Original Message-----
From: Chandrashekar Babu [mailto:lug@chandrashekar.info] 
Sent: Thursday, September 16, 2004 2:32 AM
To: Balakrishnan C
Subject: Re: [Ilugc] Project Looking Glass!

> A week back I looked at Project Looking Glass and even downloaded a
> stable build. But, unfortunately it isn't running in my computer, as
> mine doesn't qualify fit enough to run it! Anyone, here was successful
> running it? How are the looks and feel of it?

I tried getting it to work two months ago, I wasn't that impressed.
While there were nice things like rotating/rendering a window in a 3d
space, there isn't any practical use for it, and it is *slow*. For a
l33t desktop, I still would prefer the enlightenment window manager. I'm
still waiting for the functional release of e-17 (Enlightenment 0.17)
which might provide graphical eye-candy interface, with focus on some
practical usability. And yes, for most of today's machines,
enlightenment isn't "bloated" nor slow for the features it provides (it
runs peacefully on my Pentium-133 with 32 MB RAM laptop).

There was a similar project by name fresco (http://www.fresco.org), and
it seems to me that the project is either waiting for some graphics
programming wizards to pitch in, or possibly, the original developers
are figuring out what to do with it.

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Sat Sep 18 16:23:24 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Sat Sep 18 16:46:18 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] VSNL 512kbps service
Message-ID: <20040918105324.E805C32C85@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>


I made enquiries about the VSNL broadband service that's being
advertised by various agents, and here is some of the info I've
obtained:

1. There are several plans, related to the monthly download size:

a) 250 MB for Rs.500, Rs.1.75/MB above this.
b) 500 MB for Rs.875  (<- note: this is competitive with BSNL DIAS)
c) 1000 MB for Rs.1500

In all cases, there's a one-time installation charge of Rs.3500, of
which Rs.1000 is refundable.

2. It uses a dry pair (cable) that's run from their remote server site 
(something like a DSLAM) to the client. Not sure if it actually
uses standards-based DSL signalling, but it's probable. It is an
always-on, 512 kbps service.

3. You have a choice of using a USB DSL modem, or a DSL-to-Ethernet
gateway device (the latter is more useful for Linux). There's also
a router device that they're peddling for Rs.9000.

4. I asked if the line protocol was PPPoE - he didn't understand the
question, but claimed that there's both Windows and Linux support.
It seems to suggest a PPPoE connection, but it might just be NAT'ed IP
from their server.

5. It's available in some areas, including Guindy/Ekkatuthangal - it depends
on where they have their DSLAMs.

-Siva 
From linux at frodo.hserus.net  Sat Sep 18 17:19:32 2004
From: linux at frodo.hserus.net (Suresh Ramasubramanian)
Date: Sat Sep 18 17:19:43 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] VSNL 512kbps service
In-Reply-To: <20040918105324.E805C32C85@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>
References: <20040918105324.E805C32C85@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>
Message-ID: <10166.::ffff:61.11.81.249.1095508172.squirrel@webmail.hserus.net>

<quote who="Sivasankar Chander">
>
> 1. There are several plans, related to the monthly download size:
>

Some confusion here.  VSNL / Tata Indicom is now what Dishnet DSL has been
rebranded to, and they've been offering 512K ADSL for quite some time at
vastly inflated rates - these are starting to come down though.

That uses PPPoA (PPP over ATM) rather than PPPoE (PPP over Ethernet). 
PPPoE is much easier to support on linux but for PPPoA you'd need a usb
modem or a router type device.

VSNL also was, and is, offering their DIAS service, which I think uses
CorDECT from Prof Jhunjunuwala / TENET at IITM, which basically sounds
like a cut down version of ISDN the last time I checked.

Which is this?

--suresh

> 
> Some confusion here.  VSNL / Tata Indicom is now what Dishnet DSL has been
> rebranded to, and they've been offering 512K ADSL for quite some time at
> vastly inflated rates - these are starting to come down though.
> 
  Ah, so this is just the old Dishnet DSL service. The prices are far
more competitive now, though.

> That uses PPPoA (PPP over ATM) rather than PPPoE (PPP over Ethernet). 
> PPPoE is much easier to support on linux but for PPPoA you'd need a usb
> modem or a router type device.
> 
  Aargh, I'd prefer a nice, clean Ethernet interface with PPPoE, which would
allow me to use my own Linux NAT/firewall/router box.

> VSNL also was, and is, offering their DIAS service, which I think uses
> CorDECT from Prof Jhunjunuwala / TENET at IITM, which basically sounds
> like a cut down version of ISDN the last time I checked.

  No, it's BSNL which offers DIAS. It doesn't use CorDECT (which is a
wireless/cellular standard), but rather a wired connection similar to
ISDN. That's what I'm using now, and it's fine, but limited to 128 kbps.

Date: Sat Sep 18 21:04:31 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] VSNL 512kbps service - info about another competitor Iqara
References: <20040918105324.E805C32C85@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>
Message-ID: <414C5749.6020805@md4.vsnl.net.in>

Sivasankar Chander wrote:
 > I made enquiries about the VSNL broadband service that's being
 > advertised by various agents, and here is some of the info I've
 > obtained:
I have been using broadband services offered by BG Broadband India (P) L
   www.iqara.net

 >
 > 1. There are several plans, related to the monthly download size:
 >
 > a) 250 MB for Rs.500, Rs.1.75/MB above this.
 > b) 500 MB for Rs.875  (<- note: this is competitive with BSNL DIAS)
 > c) 1000 MB for Rs.1500

The cost of 326 MB for 366 days is Rs. 755/-
50% discount on Data Transfer between 10PM and 10AM
By DT they mean both bytes sent and received
Recently, they claim to have made their rates more competitive.


 >
 > In all cases, there's a one-time installation charge of Rs.3500, of
 > which Rs.1000 is refundable.
 >
The onetime installation charge is Rs. 999/- and 150 MB is free with
that valid for 30 days.

 > 2. It uses a dry pair (cable) that's run from their remote server site
 > (something like a DSLAM) to the client. Not sure if it actually
 > uses standards-based DSL signalling, but it's probable. It is an
 > always-on, 512 kbps service.

Iqara uses a DSL line that is always on.

 >
 > 3. You have a choice of using a USB DSL modem, or a DSL-to-Ethernet
 > gateway device (the latter is more useful for Linux). There's also
 > a router device that they're peddling for Rs.9000.

The DSL Line connects to an ethernet card (Rs. 300/- extra for a DAX card)

 >
 > 4. I asked if the line protocol was PPPoE - he didn't understand the
 > question, but claimed that there's both Windows and Linux support.
 > It seems to suggest a PPPoE connection, but it might just be NAT'ed IP
 > from their server.

Iqara uses PPPoE.  I think they use a MS Server at Thiruvanmiyur, and
they support both Windows and Gnu/Linux.

But, we have to "support" Gnu/Linux ourselves, by searching for the
driver for ethernet card if required, and compiling and installing
RP-PPPoE. Iqara service generally good.

But in some ways, counting bytes sent and received is taking away some
of the freedom in browsing freely.  I use iqara for _email_ only without
having to pay for a telephone call every time I check mail. But, I use
bsnl/vsnl for browsing, though it is relatively slow.

HTH.
Ramanraj.

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Sat Sep 18 23:58:36 2004
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Sun Sep 19 12:28:48 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] syntax highlighting - VI
In-Reply-To: <20040919065222.39817.qmail@web52902.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <20040919065836.34593.qmail@web50202.mail.yahoo.com>

Hi Bala Chandar:

> i am unable to highlight the syntax in vim editor.
> its always showing the black on white. how do i
> enable the colors and also syntax highlighting..

All the different color schemes for vim are located in
/usr/share/vim/vim62/colors/ directory.

Create a .vimrc in your home directory and add the
following to it (for example, if you want the pablo
color scheme):

colorscheme pablo

Regards,

Shaks

> I made enquiries about the VSNL broadband service that's being
> advertised by various agents, and here is some of the info I've
> obtained:
> 
> 1. There are several plans, related to the monthly download size:
> 
> a) 250 MB for Rs.500, Rs.1.75/MB above this.
> b) 500 MB for Rs.875  (<- note: this is competitive with BSNL DIAS)
> c) 1000 MB for Rs.1500
> 
> In all cases, there's a one-time installation charge of Rs.3500, of
> which Rs.1000 is refundable.
> 
> 2. It uses a dry pair (cable) that's run from their remote server site
> (something like a DSLAM) to the client. Not sure if it actually
> uses standards-based DSL signalling, but it's probable. It is an
> always-on, 512 kbps service.
> 
> 3. You have a choice of using a USB DSL modem, or a DSL-to-Ethernet
> gateway device (the latter is more useful for Linux). There's also
> a router device that they're peddling for Rs.9000.
> 
> 4. I asked if the line protocol was PPPoE - he didn't understand the
> question, but claimed that there's both Windows and Linux support.
> It seems to suggest a PPPoE connection, but it might just be NAT'ed IP
> from their server.
> 
> 5. It's available in some areas, including Guindy/Ekkatuthangal - it depends
> on where they have their DSLAMs.
> 
> -Siva

############################################################################

HACKERS WANTED, FSF CALLING: From the FSF-India mailing list
http://mm.gnu.org.in/mailman/listinfo/fsf-prog there's a word of advice from
Anand Babu <ab@gnu.org.in>: "Yes I am need of developers for Free Software
Projects. If you are new to FSF projects, (you can get started) like this

 	* Setup a Debian GNU/Linux system (best distro for developers)
 	* Create an account for yourself at http://savannah.gnu.org.
 	* Take a look at current GNU Task List at
   	  https://savannah.gnu.org/people/?group=tasklist

Choose one and start hacking. This process will help you prepare yourself
with the GNU's way of hacking software. Then, when you feel you are ready
for the main stream, you can jump into GNU Hurd kernel hacking (the most
important pending task).

Anand Babu <ab@gnu.org.in> said at another time: "Kernel hacking is too
difficult for newbies. I need developers with sold experience in C and
system programming with a Hacker's attitude. I would recommend newbies to
start hacking at the applications level, submitting patches, getting
familiar with GNU coding standards and Free Software development model."

############################################################################

[GNU]LINUX DEMO DAY IN DELHI:  Raj Mathur <raju@linux-delhi.org> announced
plans to hold a Linux Demo Day, organized by India Linux Users Group, Delhi
(ILUGD, www.linux-delhi.org).

 	Says Mathur: "We will   be conducting Linux-related  talks  and
 	presentations in the Hamdard Archives Auditorium, on Saturday, Sept
 	25, 2004, by some of our resident experts, and hopefully they will
 	interest people who've already taken the plunge as well as those who
 	are just about to. There'll be lots of demonstrations/talks
 	throughout the day and plenty of opportunities to gain hands-on
 	experience of different Linux distributions and applications for
 	yourself. There is space outside the auditorium, which will be used
 	for giving the demos. The demos and the talks will go on
 	concurrently. We'll also be distributing Linux goodies at low or no
 	cost.

Venue: Jamia Hamdard Archives Auditorium Hamdard University, New Delhi
110062. Landmark: Adjacent to Batra Hospital. Entry from Gate 6 Date:
September 25, 2004 Time: 10 am-6 pm (Registration at 9:30 am)
Contact: ldd2k4@linux-delhi.org Entry: Free -- all are invited.

############################################################################

PROMOTING A PROPRIETARY FORMAT, FORCING A PROPRIETARY APPLICATION: V. Sasi
Kumar <vsasi@hotpop.com> of the Centre for Earth Science Studies in Tvn
writes: "Indian Institute of Science asks alumni to fill up their details in
a document in MS Word format. This is a mail I sent them more than two weeks
back. No response as yet.

"Sir, I find that the proforma for membership records is given in a
proprietary format (MS Word) which forces me to use a proprietary
application. Indirectly you are promoting a particular company's software
that uses a closed format for its files, which is not a very good practice
for an internationally reputed institute like IISc.

"Instead, I suggest that the proforma be made available in open formats like
Postscript, PDF, XML, etc. This would enable anyone using any word processor
or any free application (like xpdf, Open Office, etc.) to read the file
without loss of formatting. May I also point out that even our President,
Dr. A.P.J. Abdul Kalam, has prompted scientists and technologists to move
from proprietary software to free software for several reasons, including
national security and economics."

 	the discussion list http://linux-bangalore.org/2004/discuss/ "

INTERNATIONAL OPEN SOURCE NETWORK: The International Open Source Network
(IOSN - http://www.iosn.net) is a Centre of Excellence for Free / Open
Source Software in the Asia-Pacific Region. IOSN is an initiative of the
Asia-Pacific Information Development Programme (APDIP -
http://www.apdip.net), which has been supporting the strategic and effective
use of Information Communication Technology (ICT) for poverty alleviation
and sustainable human development in the Asia-Pacific region since 1997. Via
a small secretariat, the IOSN is tasked specifically to facilitate and
network Free / Open Source Software advocates and human resources in the
region. Activities undertaken by IOSN is listed below:

A. Free / Open Source Information Resource Facility

      1. Collaborative Website: On-going Mapping of Free / Open Source
         activities in Asia-Pacific;  Collaborative    database     of
         countries;   languages, fonts,and organisations in Asia-Pacific;
         On-line Information/Clearing-house and Mailing Lists
      2. Software Repository: A collection of FOSS software and GNU/Linux
         distributions specific to the Asia Pacific is being created.
      3. Documentation of Best Practise
      4. Open Source Primers: General FOSS by Kenneth Wong/Phet Sayo;
         Malaysia; Licensing by Shunling Chen-Taiwan; Policy by Kenneth
         Wong; Localisation by Anousak Souphavanh / Theppitak
         Karoonboonyanan - Thailand; Network/Security/Infrastructure by
         Gaurab Raj Upadhaya - Nepal; and Education by Wooi Tong Tan -
         Malaysia.

B. Creation of a Database of Free / Open Source Experts and Human
    Resources in the Region

      1. Networking of Experts
      2. Technical Support

C. Training and Workshops

      1. FOSSAP 2004: More than 50 senior policy makers and open source
         practitioners from 20 countries attended this event.
         http://www.iosn.net/fossap/
      2. Training of Trainers: We are currently planning the first
         training in Vietnam in partnership with Linux Professional
         Institute

D. Research and Development

      1. Localisation Toolkit in collaboration with Centre for Advanced
         Computing [CDAC], India
      2. End-user training material in Text and Multimedia format. Script
         by Dr. Nah Soo Hoe, Malaysia and production by GetIT multimedia,
         Singapore.
      3. GNU/Linux Live CD Project by Colin Charles, Australia of the
         Fedora Project.
      4. Q&A on FOSS R&D/Case Studies of implementations
      5. Micro-grant Programme in collaboration with University of South
         Pacific

FROM PAKISTAN: The Open Source Resource Center (OSRC)
[http://www.osrc.org.pk] had scheduled a seminar on Free and Open Source
Software in Karachi on 14 September 2004. For registration and details,
visit http://www.osrc.org.pk/seminar/

The Open Source Resource Center (OSRC) is a first such forum in Pakistan
created by Pakistan Software Export Board (G) Ltd. [http://www.pseb.org.pk/]
at Islamabad. The Resource Center aims to bring together wide range of
expertise related to [Free/Libre and] Open Source Technologies and Resources
at one place. The IT companies can access, share, and contribute the
knowledge particular to the development and transformation of IT products on
FLOSS. The Resource Center works to bring together established technology
vendors, startups, open source community members and enterprise IT
users/customers to jointly explore new opportunities for OSS deployment and
how to capitalize on them.

############################################################################

 	PRIMER ON FLOSS, VIA MALAYSIA: IOSN has produced a primer on
 	Free/Open Source Software Licensing and an early pre-copyedited
 	draft of the primer is now available for public review and feedback.
 	This primer is an introductory summary of licensing issues involved
 	with using the different FOSS licenses, primarily the GNU GPL
 	license. It offers several scenarios, and proposes a framework for
 	licensing of government sponsored software.  The primer also
 	addresses common questions and misconceptions regarding copyright
 	and licensing issues. Further details from khairil@apdip.net
 	http://www.iosn.net/licensing/foss-licensing-primer/

SOME ASIAN G/LINKS AND GNU/LUGS: A query brought in some interesting links
to LUGs in and around Asia. Here's a listing of some:

Lanka Linux User Group (LK-LUG) has been operating since 1998.They also have
a localization project: http://sinhala.linux.lk Check out more details at
http://www.linux.lk or http://www.lug.lk

Cambodia's English-language Majordomo-based mailing-list is at
linux@forum.org.kh Once there, one can also have a look at their KhmerOS
Initiative, to create UNICODE based Khmer language software -- in both the
Windows and the Linux environments. Check out http://www.KhmerOS.info

The Iranian LUG is pretty active: http://www.farsilinux.org Saudi's mailing
list is at http://groups.yahoo.com/group/saudi_linux/

Outside this continent, but probably having shared interests is the
http://fossfa.net This is the body working to promote Free and Open Source
Software in Africa. It has some 53 member states.

############################################################################

 	THE STEPS AHEAD: Anand Babu wrote to friends from South Africa that
 	the FSF-India working group is discussing initiatives on
 	e-governance, localization and live CD distributions,
 	super-computing grid and other core GNU tasks through Free Software
 	Development Lab. Says he: "So far Government has hardly done
 	anything for the Free Software Movement in India. Here is a three
 	step approach they need to take: (1) Standardize on Free Software
 	for all Governmental use. (2) Actively support and promote (educate)
 	Free Software as #1 choice for the community (3) Fund Free Software
 	initiatives.

USEFUL SCRIPT FOR STUDENTS: Robin Turner of Bilkent Universitesi in
Ankara-Turkey <robin@bilkent.edu.tr> recently announced on the FSF-India
list that he has just updated his script for enabling students to upload
their work via a web page. Improvements: 1. Students choose which essay they
are submitting and the program automatically renames the file to something
appropriate ("this is because I am fed up with recieving files named 'My
Essay.doc'"); 2. The program now runs in taint mode and untaints submitted
variables ("I don't know if this really makes it any more secure, but it
makes me feel righteous"). If anyone wants to use it, it's at
<www.bilkent.edu.tr/~robin/scripts/101upload.cgi>.

have to drag them to the consumer court for their act of duping
customers. I've been cheated, so be warned.

From kaveraj at gmail.com  Mon Sep 20 12:17:57 2004
From: kaveraj at gmail.com (Mohan Raj)
Date: Mon Sep 20 12:18:07 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: 2.6 kernel (debian) error - Solved
In-Reply-To: <3779a1e7040918063932a55c47@mail.gmail.com>
References: <3779a1e70409120001745089c2@mail.gmail.com>
	<3779a1e7040914022139a4cae8@mail.gmail.com>
	<20040914104810.GA33675@frodo.hserus.net>
	<3779a1e704091404244822acd9@mail.gmail.com>
	<73843eae040914055655efd942@mail.gmail.com>
	<3779a1e7040918063932a55c47@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <3779a1e7040919234720bb388@mail.gmail.com>

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
> VFS: Cannot open root device "303" or unknown block(3,3)
> Please append a correct "root=" boot option
> Kernel Panic: VFS: Unable to mount root fs on unknown block (3,3)
> -----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Ok... I got the problem solved and am running a 2.6.8.1 kernel. Just
for the records  I want this scrambled-up howto to be documented.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Seeing endless conversations of users having the same problem
with no solutions, I finally decided to drop the idea of compiling
my own kernel (and boy is it humiliating; anyway i got too tired).

So i did a 

apt-get install kernel-image-xxxx 

and rebooted. Voila! The booting passed beyond the panic point into
runlevel1. Then I did a

module-assistant auto-install nvidia

to get the nvidia drivers compiled for the new kernel. 
(module-assistant is a apt-get kind of thing for installing
drivers. AFAIK it is available only for debian.)

module-assistant reported errors. I had to install
kernel-headers-xxxx; mod-assis went fine now. But the xserver refused
to start(IIRC module nvidia not found). I had to install the
all the packages recommended when module-assistant was 
doing an apt-get as part of its process. Then X went beyond that point
and now errored that it could not find the device /dev/psaux. The dev
fs seems to have been changed in 2.6. IIRC cat /proc/bus/input/devices
revealed only the keyboard. So I added mousedev and psmouse to
/etc/modules, changed /dev/psaux and all other old referneces to mouse
(2 of them totally)
to /dev/input/mice in the xconfig file  and rebooted. And  yeah..
voila.. everything is working now.. it is faster.. but the cd/dvd
writing system is broke (a reported bug). I haven't had time to
experience much of the kernel to warrant all the trouble/time.
But I am hopeful... lets see.

-- 
 Mohan

drops to abysmally slow speeds, as low as 1 to 2 kbps during daytime.
It's not broadband, for sure. You'd be better off with dialup.

In-Reply-To: <3779a1e7040919234720bb388@mail.gmail.com>

	<3779a1e7040919234720bb388@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <414EA93B.2030307@frodo.hserus.net>

Mohan Raj wrote:
> Ok... I got the problem solved and am running a 2.6.8.1 kernel. Just
> for the records  I want this scrambled-up howto to be documented.

that is the easy way out - and it should work for people who dont want 
to compile their own kernels.

one tip is to compile as many things as are absolutely essential during 
bootup (required filesystems etc) into the kernel, and compile other 
stuff (network / video etc) as modules.

another way to go would be to get a debian source package, edit the 
config file to add / remove certain options (such as removing a bunch of 
stuff compiled into the kernel that you dont use, or stopping the 
compilation of modules for a whole lot of hardware that you dont have) 
and do a make-kpkg to build a new kernel deb for your system, compiled 
to your processor instead of for i386

> doing an apt-get as part of its process. Then X went beyond that point
> and now errored that it could not find the device /dev/psaux. The dev
> fs seems to have been changed in 2.6. IIRC cat /proc/bus/input/devices
> revealed only the keyboard. So I added mousedev and psmouse to

hotplug and udevd for 2.6 .. see if you have a package called udevd or 
udev in debian and install that.

	srs

Sridhar R wrote:

> Apart from that, they have also changed there 'unlimited' plans. 
> Browsing more than 6 hours per day is not allowed.  If done so, they
> one day will be reduced from remaining validity days.  Guess, sify's
> gonna crush!!

6 hours per day limitation is applicable for only 64kbps (64-92 kbps) shared. 
For 32 kbps (32-64 kbps), they have a different restriction. Only the first 75 MB 
download of the day will operate at 32-64 kbps. Rest of the download will clock only 
at 24 kbps. It will be reset in the next day.

I talked to them and they said that users started using a lot of peer-peer sharing 
clients and keep downloading 24x7 which causes the other users to suffer.

I have opted for 9pm - 9am 128 kbps. There is no such restrictions on this plan. I 
will be connected tomorrow. I will let you know by Friday.

PS: An extremly out of topic question. Sorry for this. It seems that Sify forces 
to use Mc Afee with Windows and also forces to uninstall any other AV installed on 
the system? Any idea about this?

Suresh Ramasubramanian wrote:
> Anand Saha wrote:
> >has anyone customized Bugzilla for general purpose issue tracking ? We
> >want such a tracking system similar to the Remedy ticket tracking system.

We are just going through the process of deploying RT3 in our
orgnisation for email tracking (our customer support receives hundreds
of mail daily).  The system is going live tomorrow morning.

The reason I mention this is because I've spent the past 2 weeks
researching open sourced and commercial CRMs and nothing comes close to
RT in terms of flexibility and ease of customisation.  But be warned
that RT3 can be a pain to install due to its extensive perl module
dependencies (unless you run debian sarge ofcourse ;-)

If you do not require lengthy complex workflows, try www.otrs.org and
mailmanager.sf.net.  See
    http://linas.org/linux/pm.html
for an exhaustive list of CRM and other solutions.

- Raja

Hi,

Anand Kumar Saha wrote:
> do you need the feature of generating reports from the database ? if
> yes, what are you doing for that, as RT's site asks users to use tools
> like Crystal Report to fetch and generate reports. RT it seems doesn't 
> have this inbuild facility. (or does it?)

RT does not include builtin reports.

The "incremental search/filter" feature on the rt/Search/Listing.html
page is very flexible.  It allows you to generate several common reports
on a real-time basis.

Beyond this, my management only wanted 3 reports which we wrote some
perl code to get it together.

on freebsd its just a simple matter of doing

# cd /usr/ports/www/rt3-elixus (or rt3, or rt32 if you want rt3 / rt3.2)

# make install clean

I guess you could do "emerge sync rt3" or something on gentoo

Come to think of it, rpm is not too bad if you have rpm packages for rt 
- it is reasonably good at resolving dependencies these days.

About rt3-elixus - http://p4.elixus.org/hist/

> Developed by elixus.org and supported by OurInternet, Inc, rt3-elixus is
> a beefed-up branch based on the latest -pre/-rc/-final release of RT3.
> It features an alternate Tabbed UI, Workflow editor, many more custom field
> types (including multiple-entry fields), Object Attributes, and has been
> ported to Microsoft Windows.

From linux at frodo.hserus.net  Tue Sep 21 10:29:08 2004
From: linux at frodo.hserus.net (Suresh Ramasubramanian)
Date: Tue Sep 21 10:28:19 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Creating a .config file from a running kernel
In-Reply-To: <3779a1e7040920214845592972@mail.gmail.com>
References: <3779a1e7040920214845592972@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <414FB51C.2090008@frodo.hserus.net>

Mohan Raj wrote:
> I think that 2.6 series of kernels have a feature that makes it possible to 
> create a .config file from a running kernel. Anybody knows how to do this?

Do an ls -al in the /usr/src/linux directory (or look in /usr/src for 
your kernel version)

You will find the .config file that was used to build the kernel there

	srs

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Tue Sep 21 10:38:17 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Tue Sep 21 11:01:33 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Creating a .config file from a running kernel
In-Reply-To: <3779a1e7040920214845592972@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20040921050818.0694E329BA@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> I think that 2.6 series of kernels have a feature that makes it possible to 
> create a .config file from a running kernel. Anybody knows how to do this?
> 
  I think it needs to be compiled in; with this option, the .config shows
up somewhere on /proc (possibly /proc/config). I haven't looked at what the
entries look like. It's a pretty neat idea, but brings a whole can of worms
with it - a lot of userland programs are going to be written that adapt
dynamically at runtime to kernel options, increasing the difficulty of
validation, debugging, version control ... (maybe I'm wrong).

-Siva
From lug at chandrashekar.info  Tue Sep 21 11:05:26 2004
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar Babu)
Date: Tue Sep 21 11:06:07 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Creating a .config file from a running kernel
In-Reply-To: <3779a1e7040920214845592972@mail.gmail.com>
References: <3779a1e7040920214845592972@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20040921110526.5dea3206.lug@chandrashekar.info>

> I think that 2.6 series of kernels have a feature that makes it possible to 
> create a .config file from a running kernel. Anybody knows how to do this?

If you did "Enable access to .config through /proc/config.gz" in "General Setup" (at the 'make menuconfig', or CONFIG_IKCONFIG=y, CONFIG_IKCONFIG_PROC=y in your .config file) while compiling your 2.6 kernel, you can access your .config file of a running kernel by simply copying /proc/config.gz to a different directory and 'gunzip'-ing the same. 

Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

Quoting from their website:
Wikipedia (www.wikipedia.org) is a "copyleft" encyclopedia that is collaboratively developed using wiki software. Wikipedia is managed and operated by the non-profit Wikimedia Foundation. In addition to standard "encyclopedic" knowledge, Wikipedia includes information more often associated with almanacs and gazetteers, as well as coverage of current events.

Fundraising
Imagine a world in which every single person on the planet is given free access to the sum of all human knowledge. That's what we're doing. And we need your help.

Fund drive goal: $50,000

 $46,430.11 USD to go
 
The Wikimedia Foundation Inc. is a non-profit organization with the goal of providing free knowledge to every person in the world. Meeting this goal through the maintainence, development and distribution of free content, Wikimedia relies on public donations to run its wiki-based projects.

Wikimedia provides computing and network resources to create and distribute many reference works including Wikipedia (http://en.wikipedia.org), Wiktionary (http://en.wiktionary.org), Wikiquote (http://en.wikiquote.org), Wikibooks (http://en.wikibooks.org), Wikisource (http://wikisource.org) and the Wikimedia Commons (http://commons.wikimedia.org). The content of these projects is provided to the public free of charge.

How your donation will help
All of our sites are free from advertisements. Visitors are not charged to edit, read or use our content. We rely entirely on donations to fund our projects. Our unprecedented growth in traffic and content requires regular hardware updates to prevent outages without sacrificing functionality. Other outgoings include bandwidth costs, rackspace within a colocation center, purchase of Wikimedia's domain names, sponsorship of specific software development tasks, and, occasionally, travel expenses.

The Wikimedia Foundation also requires funding to continue its pioneering role in exploring the field of collaborative content creation. Every donation can make a big difference. 

For more information, check out http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Main_Page and http://wikimediafoundation.org/wiki/Fundraising

on the

The best way to ensure a pan-indian participation is to keep rotating the
event (like say Linux India  2004) in different state capitals every year.
Till then, LB will be a predominantly Bangalore/Southern-India centric 
event
attended by either people from nearby regions or by people who have the 
money
or time.

>>I made enquiries about the VSNL broadband service that's being
>>advertised by various agents, and here is some of the info I've
>>obtained:
>>
>>1. There are several plans, related to the monthly download size:
>>
>>a) 250 MB for Rs.500, Rs.1.75/MB above this.
>>b) 500 MB for Rs.875  (<- note: this is competitive with BSNL DIAS)
>>c) 1000 MB for Rs.1500
>>
>>In all cases, there's a one-time installation charge of Rs.3500, of
>>which Rs.1000 is refundable.
>>
>>2. It uses a dry pair (cable) that's run from their remote server site
>>(something like a DSLAM) to the client. Not sure if it actually
>>uses standards-based DSL signalling, but it's probable. It is an
>>always-on, 512 kbps service.
>>
>>3. You have a choice of using a USB DSL modem, or a DSL-to-Ethernet
>>gateway device (the latter is more useful for Linux). There's also
>>a router device that they're peddling for Rs.9000.
>>
>>4. I asked if the line protocol was PPPoE - he didn't understand the
>>question, but claimed that there's both Windows and Linux support.
>>It seems to suggest a PPPoE connection, but it might just be NAT'ed IP
>>from their server.
>>
>>5. It's available in some areas, including Guindy/Ekkatuthangal - it depends
>>on where they have their DSLAMs.
>>
>>-Siva

From arun.balaji at gmail.com  Fri Sep 24 16:52:43 2004
From: arun.balaji at gmail.com (arun balaji)
Date: Fri Sep 24 16:52:50 2004
Subject: Fwd: [Ilugc] Fwd: announcing a open source security system for linux
In-Reply-To: <e9dd6748040924042112e6177@mail.gmail.com>

	<e9dd6748040924042112e6177@mail.gmail.com>

---------- Forwarded message ----------
From: arun balaji <arun.balaji@gmail.com>
Date: Fri, 24 Sep 2004 16:51:20 +0530
Subject: Re: [Ilugc] Fwd: announcing a open source security system for linux
To: Anand Kumar Saha <anand.kumar@gavsin.com>

randover validates users and data .

practical example of randover-

-credit card authentication
-user authentication
-logins
-and more

imagine bering able to authenticate the user where the user has the
control over the login process

randover stands for (rando)m (ver)ification of user data

so randover authenticates the user via a random question.

the process is like this
step1. user registers on the site
step2. user login
 -user is asked a random question.
if answer is correct he is logged in.
if answer is wrong he is not logged in.

its just 10 lines of code that can change the way user logs into the system.

it can be used alone or integrated with existing systems

its a algorithm for user security.

bye
arun balaji

Karthik wrote:
 > i got Iqara broadband connection recently .. i configured my Ethernet

address using the ifconfig command..
 > i downloaded RP-PPPoE .. when i compiled and installed, it asked some

completed the configuration, i gave adsl-start to connect.. but i didnt 
get connected ... it also didnt give me any 'connected' messages ... it 
simply shows me the shell prompt....
 >

RP-PPPoE has a TCL/Tk based gui called tkpppoe, with which you can
easily configure and use. tkpppoe is usually found in the "gui" source
directory. Of course, you would run tkpppoe like this:

# wish tkpppoe

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Fri Sep 24 18:45:01 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Fri Sep 24 19:08:33 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] setting up Iqara Broadband connection in Linux
In-Reply-To: <20040924125451.85865.qmail@web40003.mail.yahoo.com>

> i got Iqara broadband connection recently ..

> i downloaded RP-PPPoE ..

  For RP-PPPoE, you don't need to assign a static IP address to the
eth interface (in fact, you should not). adsl-start will assign an
IP address to the PPPoE interface (say ppp0) when it connects.
