From siva at dias.ath.cx  Sat Sep 25 08:33:47 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Sat Sep 25 08:57:17 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Connect 2004 exhibition highlights
Message-ID: <20040925030347.CEAE8329BA@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>


  I visited the Connect 2004 Exhibition at the Chennai Trade Centre,
and here are the highlights - mostly gadget-focussed, I'm not really
interested in the zillion companies selling VB development services.

1. Both AMD and Intel had large booths, and AMD is emphasizing AMD64
(as expected). They trotted out a 2-CPU Celestica Opteron box, but
not a demo model, just a static showpiece. 

2. Palm was there through their local distributor. Tungstens and other
hardware were there on display.

3. The Simputer people were there at the rear, with some Simputers on
demo. Too bulky and kludgy, IMO. The build quality was about the same
as 1st-generation Taiwan-made mobiles 15 years ago.

4. AMI had a superb 1U NAS with 4 hot-swap SCSI slots and 2 Gbit Ethernet
interfaces, running embedded Linux. Pricey at Rs.1.80 lakhs without the
drives - but superb engineering. They also had a PCI MegaRAC server
management card.

5. There was an 1U dual-Xeon with an Intel 7210 motherboard and 2 hot-swap
slots. Rs.80k was the base pricing - not too expensive really, but I'd
prefer the dual Opteron 1U.

6. Lots of notebooks - Fujitsu's local distributor had brought a ton of
Pentium M notebooks, and one ultra-small Transmeta Crusoe based Lifebook.
HP brought a pen-pad and some other Pentium M notebooks. However, not a
single AMD64 mobile in sight.

7. HP had a nice USB 2.0 external 8x DVD writer for Rs.11k.

8. Benq had a bunch of stuff including a DLP projector, LCD flat-panel
TVs, etc. In fact, a lot of the booths had flat-panel TVs - looks like
it's the hot meme of the moment.

9. Finally, the creme-de-la-creme: There's a Linksys distributor from
Coimbatore who offers the Linksys WRT54G for Rs.5800! For those who
aren't familiar with the WRT54G, it's a Linux-based broadband/wireless
router that's been extensively hacked/improved by junta. If there's one
thing at the show that I immediately wanted to buy, it was the WRT54G.
I'm dying to put generic 2.4 with FreeSWAN/IPsec on it. It's ideal for
all the community mesh networks that are sprouting up all over the place.

-Siva
 
From vsst at ipr.res.in  Sat Sep 25 10:18:25 2004

Date: Sat Sep 25 10:29:01 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Compilation of a module under kernel 2.6
In-Reply-To: <20040924160940.529C61DB2D6@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <Pine.GSO.4.10.10409251011160.23152-100000@sun4.plasma.ernet.in>

   suppose your module is hello.c. Do create a makefile as follows:
        obj-m :=3D hello.o
   save it and compile it as follows:
       make -C /pathtolinuxkernelsource SUBDIRS=3D$PWD modules.

    for more info, refer kbuild in the Documentation directory of the
Linux kernel source.

> > i got Iqara broadband connection recently ..=20
> > I also assigned a static IP address using the ifconfig command..
> > i downloaded RP-PPPoE ..
>=20
>   For RP-PPPoE, you don't need to assign a static IP address to the
> eth interface (in fact, you should not). adsl-start will assign an
> IP address to the PPPoE interface (say ppp0) when it connects.
>=20

From vsst at ipr.res.in  Sat Sep 25 10:25:36 2004
From: vsst at ipr.res.in (S.Thayumanavar)
Date: Sat Sep 25 10:36:10 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Module Compilation Under 2.6 Kernel
In-Reply-To: <20040924160940.529C61DB2D6@www.ae.iitm.ac.in>
Message-ID: <Pine.GSO.4.10.10409251022180.23364-100000@sun4.plasma.ernet.in>


	suppose you have a module simple.c, to compile create a makefile
with the contents as
     obj-m := simple.o
Then type at shell as make -C pathtokernelsource(2.6) SUBDIRS=$PWD modules
   then insmod simple.ko
More info can be found in the kbuild.txt file in Documentation directory
of the kernel.

On Sat, 25 Sep 2004 15:07:54 +0530, Tarun Kumar <tarun@anadocs.com> wrote:
> Hi,
> How do I install a GUI Desktop (KDE or GNOME) from text console.
> I already have Redhat Linux 7.3 running on the system with nothing related
> to graphics installed.

You could upgrade your system using the RedHat 7.3 CDs itself and
install everything required.

Then when the system starts up(if you havent changed it to start in
graphics mode) then change the default runlevel to 5 in /etc/inittab.

Reboot.

I think it should work.

From praveen at symonds.net  Sat Sep 25 21:52:28 2004
From: praveen at symonds.net (Praveen)
Date: Sat Sep 25 21:53:32 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT]My experience with SIfy broadband.
Message-ID: <41559B44.6050807@symonds.net>

For the past few days, there are quite a lot of discussions going on in 
ILUGC mailing list about various broadband services. Yesterday I got 
Sify broadband for my home PC. I thought that it would be of some use to 
share my experience with Sify.

I am residing at Chinmaya Nagar, Virugambakkam. The main reason that I 
went for Sify is that there was no other service provider in my area 
(ignoring dial-up). Touchtel is not having copper in this area. No Hathway.

The installation charge was INR. 3000. Since I had my own ehternet card 
(nVidia nForce MCP), I haven't paid that extra INR.500 for the ethernet 
adapter. The way the wire the PC is through RJ45 cable. The nearest 
switch from my home was about 130m. They used CAT 5E cable. My PC runs 
Fedora Core 2 and Microsoft Windows 2000 Professional. The dealer said 
that he will configure the Windows network setup for me so that I can 
use the same thing for Linux as well. He was having no idea of Linux. My 
PC was given 10.x.x.x IP address and he gave me a couple of nameservers 
to use. Once the Windows network setup was completed, he went to one of 
the Sify login servers and downloaded the Sify login tool for Windows. 
While starting the setup, it asked to uninstall the Norton Antivirus 
2004 that I had on my system. It forced me to use McAfee virus scanner. 
I said to the dealer that I don't want to use McAfee, instead I would 
like to stay with the exisiting NAV 2004. He called up some technical 
guys mananging the firewall (sify's) sitting at Tidel park to change the 
policy for my IP address. Once they did it I installed the Sify login 
tool without any problem.

The dealer then logged in using his account and created a user name for 
me. I bought the package "9pm to 9am, 128kbps, unlimited bandwidth". It 
costs INR. 360. The dealer left once everything was working fine.

Then I rebooted into Fedora Core 2. Once I got up the prompt, I was 
shocked to see the ethernet link status as disconnected. I was wondering 
why it is so. Again I rebooted into Windows and found that it was 
working. I struggled for more than 15 minutes and later I found that the 
problem was because that the speed setting of the card was in 
"Autonegotiate" mode. Then I changed it to "10BaseT-HD" using 'mii-tool' 
after which the link was up. I downloaded the login tool for Linux from 
their login server. Tried once under Fedora, suceeded and rebooted. I 
have tested the speed both in Windows and Fedora. It was ranging from 
120-128kbps. So far so good.

Then I inserted my Debian 3.0r1 installation CD, installed the core 
system and immediately upgraded to the Sarge with my local Sarge CD set 
which is almost one year old. After which, I pointed apt to the 
Singapore Debian mirror and did a dist-upgrade. Then I installed Gnome 
(2.6) and KDE over Internet. Throughout the installation, the speed was 
ranging from 15.8 kBps to 16kBps. Absolutely good. Last night itself, I 
downloaded around 600 MB without any problem. Not even a single 
disconnection.

I am more than happy with this product. True value for INR. 360.

Just my 2 cents.

Praveen.

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Mon Sep 27 10:54:20 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Mon Sep 27 11:18:07 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] How to compile for .ko module?
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0409271029240.23805-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>
Message-ID: <20040927052420.9AF33329BA@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> > In Olitec, modem driver is compiled as e2.o module. When I load
> > e2.o, it says "Invalid module format".  Since my linux is 2.6.8.1
> > which can load only .ko module, I need to Please let me know how to
> > convert (compile)  this module as e2.ko.
> 
> I hope, modules.txt, in Documentation dir of your kernel src, will 
> explain this.

  Perhaps Olitec supplied a binary-only module, e2.o, for some
specific 2.4.x kernel. In that case, there's no easy way to make
it work on 2.6.

  OTOH, if there's a GPLed driver, it can be ported to 2.6 with some
effort - the main benefit of FLOSS.

  In general, you should completely avoid buying hardware for which
there is no GPLed driver, to avoid situations like this. Try
writing to Olitec and complaining, if there's no open-source driver.

-Siva

From karthick.sundararajan at wipro.com  Mon Sep 27 14:44:51 2004
From: karthick.sundararajan at wipro.com (karthick.sundararajan@wipro.com)
Date: Mon Sep 27 14:45:35 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] duration of connection
Message-ID: <B99FECA7782B834AB0D4D5B18D89F5F00199093D@chn-gdy-msg.wipro.com>


Just copy the following to a script:

_________________________________________________
#!/bin/bash

case $1 in
	'login')
		rconnect <username> <password>
		if [ $? -ne 0 ]
		then
			date >> /var/log/reliance.log
		fi;;
	'logout')
		rdisconnect
		if [ $? -ne 0 ]
		then
			date >> /var/log/reliance.log
		fi;;
esac
_________________________________________________

	That must help... Provided rconnect and rdisconnect return 0.

	To check this:
$ rconnect <uname> <passwd>

On successful login:
$ echo $?

	Use the value printed here in the place of 0 in the script.

	Cheers,
	Karthick S.
	Mobile Number: 9884025911
	Home Page: www.geocities.com/sksatyam

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Mon Sep 27 17:31:24 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Mon Sep 27 17:55:09 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] diff:unix and Linux
In-Reply-To: <BAY1-F9XbgESvBp8ZKx0000c1a3@hotmail.com>
Message-ID: <20040927120124.33E9D329BA@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> 
> I would like to know how Linux and Unix differ technically from 
> implementation point of view----like what are the basic differences between 
> Linux and Unix---if any.
> 
  You'll need to read the Lion's annotated commentary on Unix and similar
books on the Linux kernel (like the Coriolis Press Core Linux Kernel
commentary) to understand the differences. However, I'll summarize a
few:

1. Unix was written for the DEC PDP-7 as a simple time-sharing OS alternative
to the Multics OS. It was subsequently ported to various other platforms,
including the PDP-11, DEC VAX-11, various AT&T and NCR systems, etc.
You can get an idea of its history at the Unix history page:

http://www.levenez.com/unix

Linux, OTOH, was specifically targetted at the Intel 80386 CPU, and was
designed as a POSIX-compliant monolithic OS with support for virtual
memory. Most of the device drivers initially supported only PC/AT 
peripherals.

2. Unix did not originally have TCP/IP networking support - this work was
done at UC Berkeley and does not belong to the AT&T codebase. Linux has
had TCP/IP networking support from a very early stage in its development.

3. Linux was dependent on the GNU environment (OS, compilers, tools, etc.)
for development as well as a self-hosting platform and is still critically
dependent on it for most applications. OTOH, Unix had a pre-existing
environment that predates the GNU project.

  (In simpler terms, GNU and Linux are symbiotic; whereas proprietary
Unices have their own userland, which in some cases can be replaced by a
GNU userland).

> 
> Also I would like to know how a major number of a device file is used to 
> identify a driver .
> 
  Basically, a driver registers itself with the kernel, at initialization
time, identifying the major number it will handle. Subsequent operations
performed on that device file will result in a syscall into the kernel
which will then transfer control to that driver.
 
-Siva

Ankit Malhotra wrote: 
,----
| I would like to know  how to handle multiple select entries correctly.
| Is there no way i can avoid them from being over written. Theni have
`----

You can use an array for the name. ex:

<select name=choices[] multiple>
<option value=1>a</option>
<option value=2>b</option>
...
</select>

Now you will get all the selected values across in your PHP code.

,----
| variable number of sent in check boxes. The whole problem is that the
`----

Same with Checkboxes. Use name=choices[].  Of course, you will have to
dynamically create the checkboxes, something like:

foreach ($values as $key => $value) {
	echo "<input type=checkbox value=$key> $value\n";
}

,----
| Regarding  text area  how to  manipulate the  new line  and  line feed
| correctly. so that the line changes in display also as in input.
`----

What display?  you mean when you  'echo' whatever textarea  out in PHP
you dont see the multilines? use '<pre>' in that case.

cheers,

  -Suraj

| M. S. Subbulakshmi is a student of Semmangudi Srinivasa Iyer

From trshash84 at gmail.com  Mon Sep 27 22:11:23 2004
From: trshash84 at gmail.com (Shashwath T.R.)
Date: Tue Sep 28 19:44:49 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] diff:unix and Linux
In-Reply-To: <20040927143436.10798.qmail@mailweb33.rediffmail.com>
References: <20040927143436.10798.qmail@mailweb33.rediffmail.com>
Message-ID: <a8427db004092715113076eb01@mail.gmail.com>

Basically, the original Unix spawned the definition of POSIX or
Portable Operating System standards. These standards were then used by
many OSs, including the Mac OS X and BeOS. Among these was Linux, the
kernel, and GNU the toolset.

So, in essence, Linux is a clone of the Unix that works on the x86
(and now, many other processors). Or, if you prefer it, an
implementation of the POSIX standards.

Shash

From srinivasg at esntechnologies.co.in  Tue Sep 28 12:08:34 2004
From: srinivasg at esntechnologies.co.in (Srinivas G.)
Date: Tue Sep 28 20:00:11 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] RE: [TwinCLinG] diff:unix and Linux
Message-ID: <4EE0CBA31942E547B99B3D4BFAB34811108021@mail.esn.co.in>

Hi Chaitanya,

> Also I would like to know how a major number of a device file is used
to
> identify a driver.

The major number is useful in creating a DEVICE NODE. One of the
parameters to the command mknod is the major number. The device node is
useful to access the device related things. 

For more details please go through the 3rd chapter of Linux Device
Driver by Rubini 2nd Edition.

Regards,
Srinivas G

Hi Vikram,

Here is my successful implementation of 2..4x to 2.6.8.1.. hope this may 
be useful to u also... here is my previous message for the procedure i 
adapted.


> Thanks my dear friends, for your support! I have successfully upgraded 
> my kernel from 2.4.18.X to 2.6.8.1. it is working fine, i can feel 
> some good improvement in speed also.. ( is it so, or is it to my blind 
> eye?...   )
>
> After long struggling as a newbie, At last i followed a simple method 
> which made my job easy. i.e
> 1. copy the 2.4.18.X's .config file to 2.6.8.1's root directory (THIS 
> STRATEGY HELPED ME TO SOLVE THE DEVICE DRIVER LOADING ISSUES FOR MOST 
> OF THE HARDWARES - Here only I had got stuck up previously!!!!)
> 2. run "make menuconfig" on copied .config and add a additional 
> features or missing features carefully.
> 3. Then "make bzImage; make modules; make modules_install; make install".
> 4. If you don't use grub,  make an entry for new kernel in 
> /etc/lilo.conf and run "lilo"
>
> Hope it may be useful for others also.

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Wed Sep 29 10:21:27 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Wed Sep 29 10:45:16 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Installation Issue - Fedora Core 2 on External HDD
In-Reply-To: <415A3995.000001.01008@SITHALADEVI>
Message-ID: <20040929045127.B2F68329BA@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

>  
>  
> 7. My existing of the Laptop with 40 GB only showed. This HDD contains Win
> XP Professional Dual Boot with Fedora Core 2.
> 8. Out of 40 GB, 6 GB is allocated for Fedora Core 2.
> 9. If I boot into my Fedora Core 2 using the Grub option, then in the System
> Information - Hard Disks I find the USB Drive detected as follows:
> sad, sda1, sda2, sda3, and rest of the unallocated space of 80 GB.
>  
> Purpose:
> I want to remove the Fedora Core 2 Installation from Laptop and dedicate one
> separate HDD for the Fedora Core 2. Started of doing this when was not able
> to compile the Kernel due to insufficient space in my Laptop HDD.
>  
  The simplest option is to just forget about the external hard disk, and
use more space from the internal 40 GB hard disk for the existing Fedora
install. You can either completely blow away the Windows XP partition, or
resize it using FIPS (if you're using a FAT partition for XP). Add
an additional Linux partition with fdisk, format it using mkfs and make
it mountable using fstab - and you're home free.

  The second option is to use the remaining space on the USB hard drive
for an additional, mountable, Linux filesystem for a sub-directory, say
/home/build or something. This is not going to be suitable for any
I/O intensive work, like kernel rebuilding, because it's sitting on
USB-attached storage. It's not worth trying to use it as a root filesystem
either (in case you want to put the entire distro on it).

  You don't need to re-install Fedora for either of these options. (In
general, it's never necessary to re-install a Linux distro from scratch.
If you think you need to do that, you probably don't understand what you
want to do.)


-Siva

From: rsubr at pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au (Raja Subramanian)
Date: Wed Sep 29 17:57:05 2004

In-Reply-To: <20040927225840.69301.qmail@web8406.mail.in.yahoo.com>

Message-ID: <20040929122654.GC843@pcomm.hfi.unimelb.edu.au>

Hi,


gaurav chaturvedi wrote:
>   just a request could you guys please download the seti screensaver
>   its pritty cool and it helps process the data recived by seti
>   project 

Here are some reasons *not* to run seti -

 1. Seti's source code is not published.  For all you know, you could
    doing nuclear bomb simulation and not be searching for ET in your
    PC.

 2. A modern CPU consumes ~80W of electricity under full load.  When
    your CPU is idle, Linux puts your cpu to low power state (~4W)
    If you keep your CPU usage constantly at 100% by running seti -
        a. you get a big electricity bill,
        b. you overheat your computer and will cause premature failure
           of HDD, motherboard and CPU.

 3. Seti is a potential security risk  - seti has been hacked in the
    past.

 4. You buy a fast PC for you to use and enjoy.  Not to donate to other
    projects.  Running seti is not free and you are footing someones
    research bills.

 5. Running seti on your office pc is a good way to lose your job.


- Raja

Raja> Here are some reasons *not* to run seti -

To add Raja's comments, I'd rather be interested in donating my CPU
cycles for something more productive (say, to empower a cluster that
might help GPS tracking, weather forecast, rural education, agricultural
infrastructure or anything more practical) than wasting it to help some
research project which _can_ be dubious, and merely pointless. Is it so
important for us to establish alien contact at all (i.e., even if it stands to
be practically possible - which I personally doubt) when we (human race)
have so much to do, in order to progress towards our own stability and
sustainability for the generations to come ?


Cheers,
Chandrashekar Babu.

> Are there any other projects can steal CPU cycles like SETI...?

http://www.distributed.net/ does something similar... but for a
different purpose altogether. I'm sure thare are many others (A search
on google lists quite a lot of them).

Of course, a couple of Windows worms are programmed to do what SETI does
technically... but with bad intent - use your resources and CPU cycles
to perform a DDoS attack on a victim host (from the internet) on a
trigger.

> I also found other open source advocates on the web trying to find
> out why they couldn't stop MSNbot using a standard robots.txt
> directive in the root directory of their web sites. Some of the
> complaints related to increased fees for bandwidth.
> 
> In this article, I discuss the issue. I will also post the fix we
> discovered by accident. BTW, a standard redirect will not work.
> 
> I'm not very pleased to discover Microsoft is manipulating the
> content on the Internet.
> 
> Tom Adelsten

Bye :)
-- 
Bharathi S

Subject: [Ilugc] Help - Installing Linux with win2000

Hi,
Some time back, there was only Win98 in my machine.
I installed redhat Linux 7.2  in the Windows Filesystem itslef(FAT32).
That is, without creating any separate partition for Linux. The whole
Linux would  sit as a large single file in Windows and that large file can
be seen  through the Windows explorer itself. If I want to load Linux, I
will  insert the boot floppy of  linux(which I created during
installation). Otherwise the system will load Windows 98.

Presently I have a system with 40 gb hard disk and windows 2000 loaded in
it. The hard disk is partitioned as 4gb, 18 gb and 18 gb. (The filesystem
is NTFS in windows 2000 I guess).

I want to install any distro of linux in the current machine which has got
windows 2000.The problem is that, I cannot and dont want to repartition my
hard disk(Dont want to use third party tools like partition magic too).

So, I want to install linux with / in windows 2000 as  I had installed
with the machine which was having Win98(As in the first paragraph of this
mail).

I think most of the distros does not support to be installed in NTFS
partition.

If anybody knows any distro which can be installed as a single large file
in Win 2000 and can be booted through floppy disk(without modifying master
boot record) please tell me.

(Correct me if any of my understanding is wrong).

Thanks and regards
carti

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Thu Sep 30 15:01:22 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Thu Sep 30 15:25:23 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Help - Installing Linux with win2000
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.58.0409300427260.16768@chi.spunge.org>
Message-ID: <20040930093122.2B6C7329BA@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> Some time back, there was only Win98 in my machine.
> I installed redhat Linux 7.2  in the Windows Filesystem itslef(FAT32).
> That is, without creating any separate partition for Linux. The whole
> Linux would  sit as a large single file in Windows and that large file can
> be seen  through the Windows explorer itself. If I want to load Linux, I
> will  insert the boot floppy of  linux(which I created during
> installation). Otherwise the system will load Windows 98.
> 
  I don't think it could have been RedHat 7.2 - this was probably Xandros
or Lindows or something similar.

> So, I want to install linux with / in windows 2000 as  I had installed
> with the machine which was having Win98(As in the first paragraph of this
> mail).
> 
  It can't be done, NTFS is not write-safe in Linux. So there's no way that
the booted Linux system can write data back into the NTFS partition. You can
probably cook up a initrd-based, ramdisk-only
distro that can be booted using loadlin.exe from Windows, but it's still
going to be 3 or 4 files, and will only work from 95/98/ME if at all. You
can probably pack all of the files into a self-extracting executable to
make it a single-file executable, but it's a huge compromise on
functionality. Any changes that you make still can't be saved on a ramdisk-
only distro.

 Instead of all this, you can simply use Knoppix and boot from CDROM each
time.

-Siva

From ksriram at gmx.net  Thu Sep 30 16:27:42 2004

Ok - I really couldn't make much sense of that article - but the general
premise seems to be that MSN Bot is crashing open source sites by spidering
them..or something like that. Err..I thought it was a spider and that was it
was supposed to do. A little bit of googling on MSN Bot would tell you that

- Its in beta. You cannot view the results yet(techpreview.search.msn.com
comes up now and then when they have a new release)

- A bit of googling on webmaster forums would also show that webmasters
grudgingly accept that the MSN Bot is pretty polite and follows robots.txt
religiously..and also supports extra directives where you (the webmaster)
can specify how frequently you should be crawled


But the article does deserve some reading - I've been reading it for 15 mins
and still can't make sense of it. A good example is the following para 

<quote>
..One of the things I have discovered about Microsoft is how innovative they
can be. In my research and activities, I have uncovered some remarkable
things about a lot of companies and people. Would you find it surprising if
some open source advocates were on the payrolls of commercial companies?
What about discovering that all those articles about MSN search technology
competing with Google simply gave MSN a search bot for manipulating the
knowledge base of the Internet? The question is strictly one of conjecture;
just a question for the sake of argument and to stimulate discussion about
things people can do with technology..
</quote>

Huh?

Sriram

If the driver is for 2.4.x kernel, then you can use it
only for that major version of the kernel. If you want
to write your own Makefile for 2.6, you will have to
modify the driver as well.

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Thu Sep 30 19:25:45 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Thu Sep 30 19:49:43 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Microsoft's FAT patent overturned
Message-ID: <20040930135545.6A167329BA@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

As the subject line says, Microsoft's patent on the FAT filesystem
has been overturned by the USPTO on re-examination.

http://www.pubpat.org/Microsoft_517_Rejected.htm

This is good news in embedded space, as well as for users of digicams,
mp3 players, etc., most of which make some use of the FAT filesystem.

-Siva

From siva at dias.ath.cx  Thu Sep 30 20:13:02 2004
From: siva at dias.ath.cx (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Thu Sep 30 20:37:00 2004
Subject: [Ilugc] Microsoft's FAT patent overturned
In-Reply-To: <20040930202552.34dabe1e.lug@chandrashekar.info>
Message-ID: <20040930144302.3A75F329BA@whitebox.dias.ath.cx>

> 
> On the other hand, Microsoft has won patents for double-clicking using
> the mouse, and also for the application of the mouse scroll wheel -

 There's too much prior art for double-clicking. As far as the scroll wheel
goes, they're welcome to their patent - I've never used the scroll wheel
on any mouse.

 OTOH, the FAT patent had a lot of potential to be disruptive, because it
would have given them a stranglehold on connecting Digicams and mp3 players
to any PC, as well as on USB flash drives of any kind. That's all history
now. 

-Siva
